International Commercial Telegrams 69

丨Reuters Special Commercial Telegram, August 3rd丨

Gold and Silver: London Gold Price: The London gold price fell by half a penny today to 138 shillings and 1.5 pence.

London Silver: The London silver market was stable today, with purchases from the United States and India and sales from China. The spot price is 20.5 pence, down 0.0625; the forward price is 20.5625 pence, down 0.125.

New York Silver: The opening price of the silver market here today for forward contracts was down 15 to 35 pounds from yesterday's closing price.

Bombay Silver: The Bombay silver market was quiet today, with prices trending downward. Spot and August contracts both fell by 2 rupees to 57 rupees 12 annas; the September contract fell by 3 rupees to 57 rupees 13 annas.

Exchange Rates: British and American: The London foreign exchange market was still quiet today. The opening exchange rate for British and American was 5.03625, down 0.125 from yesterday's closing rate for US-British exchange. At 11:00 AM, it fell again by 0.1875, but rebounded by 0.125 at 2:00 PM to 5.035625. Also, one US dollar is equivalent to 3 shillings 11.661 pence in British currency.

British and French: There was no change in the opening price, remaining at 56 francs 40. At 12:00 PM, it fell by 6 pounds to 76 francs 34, but at 1:00 PM, it rose by 3 pounds to 76 francs 124. The price remained unchanged at 2:00 PM.

US-British: The New York foreign exchange market continued to be quiet this morning. The opening exchange rate for US-British was 5.035, down 0.25 from yesterday's closing price. At 10:30 AM, it rose by 0.25, then rose again by 0.125 to 5.03875.

Cotton and Wheat: American Cotton: The cotton market opened down 3 pounds. There were some sales. The price fluctuated slightly in the morning. The latest price is up 2 pounds from the opening price.

Indian Cotton: Cotton merchants in Bombay are waiting for the release of the US Department of Agriculture's cotton production report. The price of white Rohilla cotton for the April-May period is 127.5 rupees, up 0.5 rupees.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market remained firm today. At 1:00 PM, the price for October was 5 shillings 11.25 pence, up 0.375 from yesterday's closing price.

(2) President Roosevelt's imminent return to Washington and the Treasury Department's announcement of the issuance of silver certificates have once again aroused demand for government bonds with inflationary characteristics. The factors unfavorable to the market were: (1) Merchants are still closely watching the development of the European situation. (2) Market prices rebounded, but without lasting strength. The market was firm when the stock exchange opened today, with prices slightly higher. Various securities mostly rose slightly, and the bullish trend of yesterday seemed to be unfolding.

The Capture of Key Bandit Kong Hechong 84

Has been handed over by the West Route Army to Nanchang

Root of Great Evil Removed from Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan

Jiujiang Communication: Kong Hechong, a bandit leader whose power, position, and title were comparable to those of Zhu De, Mao Zedong, Peng Dehuai, He Long, Xu Xiangqian, and Fang Zhimin among the communists, was recently captured alive by the West Route Army. The center of gravity of the Red bandits in the Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan border area has been lost, and a root of great evil has been removed from the three provinces. The situation is recorded as follows:

After the Zhu, Mao, and Peng factions of the Communist bandits shifted their targets from southwestern Jiangxi to southeastern Jiangxi, they assigned Kong Hechong to be responsible for the rear guard, appointing Kong as the commander-in-chief of the puppet Sixth Army Group, commanding the puppet Jiangxi-Hubei-Hunan and Jiangxi-Hunan Military Regions. His troops included the puppet 16th, 17th, and 18th Armies, as well as the Independent 1st, 2nd, and 3rd Divisions and bandit gangs in Jiangxi-Hubei border, Jiangxi-Hunan border and other places. The puppet independent regiments and guerrilla teams of the 42 counties under the jurisdiction of the West Route Army were also under Kong's control, totaling no less than 70,000 to 80,000 people, with approximately 50,000 to 60,000 guns. The sole task of the Kong bandit was to destroy the Hunan-Hubei and Nanchang-Jiujiang railways, obstruct transportation on the Yangtze and Gan Rivers, disrupt the rear defenses of the National Army, and contain the National Army's encirclement and suppression. However, since the West Route Army has been continuously encircling and suppressing, implementing relentless pursuit, strict blocking, and tight encirclement, the bandit area of the Kong bandit has shrunk daily, and its strength has decreased. Key bandits such as Gao Yongsheng, the commander of the puppet 16th Army, have been captured, Yi Yong, the president of the puppet Red Army School, and Li Youjun, the political director of the puppet 16th Army, have surrendered one after another. Yu Xingzhou, the commander of the puppet Independent 3rd Division, has also been captured alive recently. With defeats but no victories, the generals were defeated, and the soldiers were lost. Kong was removed by the puppet central government in Ruijin from all puppet positions as commander-in-chief of the Sixth Army Group and the Three-Province Border Military Region, and was ordered by Zhu Mao to be transferred to Ruijin to serve in a certain empty puppet position. After receiving the order, Kong disguised himself and secretly fled along the Jiangxi-Hubei border to western Jiangxi, attempting to sneak across the Gan River in Taihe and Wan'an on the west bank of the Gan River, and enter Ruijin via Xingguo. However, in the middle section of the Gan River, in the Wan'an and Taihe area, the transportation between the bandits on both sides of the river could still be carried out secretly in the past due to the thin strength of the National Army. Since the National Army □Column □□Army □□Division joined the middle section of the Gan River, the defense has become more consolidated than before, and the blockade is also tighter. Therefore, when the Kong bandit was about to cross the Gan River, he was captured by a sentry of the 36th Army of the West Route. After being identified as Kong Hechong, he was properly sent to Nanchang by the army. He is currently still in the province and is being treated with great courtesy. A chief of staff of a certain division had an old relationship with Kong and had a long conversation with him. Kong revealed his regret for not doing the right thing in the first place. It is heard that after being questioned by a senior military organ, he may be given a chance to reform himself, so as to serve as a raft for ferrying the bandits in the three-province border area out of hell and into heaven.

According to news from Ji'an, Kong's strength in the Jiangxi-Hubei border area has been reduced by more than half in recent years, and there is no way to escape. The orders from the puppet central government are also extremely strict, requiring him to atone for his sins, otherwise he will be executed. Kong was in a dilemma, with no way to advance or retreat. The only way to survive was to surrender, but there was no opportunity. A certain division was transferred to Wan'an, and Kong and its chief officer had a student relationship. Therefore, he resolutely surrendered to the chief officer. Therefore, when a certain division escorted Kong to the 36th Army, he was treated with great courtesy. When escorted to Nanchang, he was treated as a guest. Some people saw him playing bamboo chess in a certain place, feeling very content. It is heard that Kong will serve the National Army to make up for his past mistakes. (July 28)

British Efforts in Far East Defense 85

Centered on the Malay Peninsula

The Entire Island Will Be Dotted with Airfields

Singapore Special Dispatch: In my previous dispatch, "The Southern British and Dutch Territories' Defense Amidst the Emergency Atmosphere of World Affairs," I already reported to my compatriots the active preparations for war by Britain and the Netherlands in their East Asian colonies. Now, I will cite another incident to further corroborate this. What is this incident? It is the British plan to implement a new aviation program throughout the Malay Peninsula. According to the general outline of this plan, from the southern tip to the northern end of the Malay Peninsula, an airfield will be built every fifty miles, densely covering the entire island with airfields. In the event of an emergency, aircraft will be used as an important tool for defending territory. Readers who have studied the general trend of the world on a daily basis should not find it difficult to understand that the reason why British power can expand so much in the Far East is entirely due to the strength of its colonies. Among Britain's colonies in East Asia, the most notable are Hong Kong, Australia, Malaya, and India. If we consider the current state of Anglo-Japanese antagonism, Hong Kong is closest to Japan. If Britain and Japan unfortunately engage in warfare, Hong Kong will be on the front line. However, Hong Kong is only a small island, unable to be self-sufficient in food and everything else, making it difficult to defend for long. Therefore, although Britain pays close attention to Hong Kong's defense, it must also plan for a place of retreat. Although Australia's position is also very important, it is ultimately shielded by the Philippines, Borneo, New Guinea, and other islands, making it difficult for Japan to invade. Therefore, at present, the most important of Britain's Far Eastern colonies is none other than Malaya. Firstly, because the area is very close to Britain's lifeline, India. Secondly, because Singapore Island in Malaya is a hub for Eurasian transportation and a key point in Britain's Three S Policy. Therefore, if Malaya encounters any unforeseen events, not only will Britain's position in India be shaken, but Britain's colonies in the Far East may also be disjointed. Therefore, the British government's gaze must focus on Malaya and regard Malaya as the center of British defense in the Far East.

Britain's deployment in Malaya did not begin today, but it has become more active since the September 18th Incident. For example, spending tens of millions of pounds to construct Singapore's naval harbor. After the completion of the harbor, the British navy in the Far East will have a very strong base, and there will be no worries. However, what Britain is currently most concerned about is strictly guarding against air strikes from other countries. At the same time, it also plans to use air power to supplement the inadequacy of naval and land forces. This is why the new aviation plan for the entire Malay Peninsula has recently been launched.

The national character of the world's peoples is different. Peoples who like to exaggerate will always boast first when doing things, which easily arouses suspicion from others. However, the British prefer to remain silent. Before achieving considerable success in anything, they will never utter a word lightly. We can see this from the attitude of Air Commodore Smith of the British Far East Air Command. Smith has been in Singapore for a long time, but he has never given a public statement. He only recently announced this plan to the press, which shows that Britain has a firm grasp on this new plan and is making progress.

In fact, the aviation industry in Malaya has made considerable progress recently. For example, airplanes flying from the Netherlands to its colony of Java must stop in Singapore. The Imperial Airways has further reduced the flight time from London to Singapore to eight days. The long-distance flight from Singapore to Australia is scheduled to commence on December 11th of this year. The British Air Ministry has also successfully mapped the aeronautical charts of the South Seas Islands, and aviation clubs have been established in Singapore, Kuala Lumpur, and Penang for civilians interested in aviation to study. Moreover, the airfield facilities from Alor Setar to Singapore are extremely well-equipped. Airfields in Sungai Petani, Penang, Taiping, Ipoh, Kuala Lumpur, Sitiawan, Port Klang, Sungai Nibong, Batu Pahat, and Malacca have been completed or are under planning along the entire route. Therefore, it should not be difficult to build an airfield every fifty miles throughout the Malay Peninsula. What are our compatriots thinking in light of other countries' active preparations for aviation?

Stalled Negotiations for Joint Sino-Japanese Transportation 86

Sogo Returns to Tokyo, South Manchuria Railway's Revenue Not Strong Last Year

If Joint Transportation is Implemented, a Large Number of Products from the Puppet State Will Enter Customs

Beijing Dispatch: Since the opening of through traffic between Peiping and Shenyang, the Japanese side has repeatedly requested joint transportation between the Peiping-Liaoning Railway and the South Manchuria Railway. It was originally intended to resume passenger transport on August 1st, followed by freight transport. Currently, due to incomplete procedures, the joint transportation issue has been shelved. Details from various parties are recorded as follows:

Hamaoto's Statement: According to Hamaoto, the information director of the South Manchuria Railway's Peiping branch, "Regarding the joint transportation issue between the South Manchuria and Peiping-Liaoning Railways, although I am a civil servant, I have not heard of any arrangements. The talk of starting joint transportation on August 1st is in the past. Joint transportation is not possible at the moment. Our country hopes to resume joint transportation as soon as possible to facilitate transportation and develop the industries of China, Japan, and 'Manchukuo'. It is untrue that Sogo, director of the South Manchuria Railway, came to Peiping to discuss joint transportation with Minister Gu of your country. Sogo's term expired on July 17th, and he is no longer a director of the South Manchuria Railway. Naturally, he cannot represent the South Manchuria Railway in negotiating joint transportation with China. Today, I received a telegram from Sogo stating that he has safely arrived in Tokyo. The South Manchuria Railway has extensive business development, and besides managing the railway itself, it also has economic enterprises in the railway-affiliated areas. Therefore, the successor to Director Sogo will be handled by personnel dispatched from the Ministry of Finance in Tokyo, and the candidate is still unknown. The South Manchuria Railway's revenue was not good last year. The only reason is the global economic panic and undeveloped industries. International transportation is naturally not smooth. Also, since the September 18th Incident, passenger and freight joint transportation between the South Manchuria Railway and the Peiping-Liaoning Railway has been suspended. Sino-Japanese commerce cannot proceed by land transportation. Therefore, the South Manchuria Railway's revenue is even more depressed than before," etc.

Pros and Cons of Joint Transportation: According to news from related parties, the Japanese economy suffered a major blow after the suspension of joint transportation between the Peiping-Liaoning and South Manchuria Railways. Therefore, the Japanese side is requesting a speedy resumption of joint transportation. If joint transportation can indeed be resumed, then the products of the puppet organization will be continuously transported into customs. The main products are: Liaoning Province has sable, otter, elk, deer, rabbit, monkey, fox, cattle, horses, sheep, sturgeon, beluga, carp, salmon, beans, wheat, millet, sorghum, potatoes, peanuts, indigo, tobacco, coal, and iron. Jilin Province has pine, fir, birch, cypress, pheasant, dove, hawk, eagle, copper, iron, and coal. Heilongjiang has donkey, mule, cattle, sheep, horse, swine, bear, tiger, squirrel, fox, sable, fish, soybeans, wheat, sorghum, corn, willow, scholar tree, elm, gold, coal, and pond salt. All can be transported by rail into the various provinces of North China for brisk sales. It is estimated that our country loses more than five million yuan annually.

Joint Transportation Stations: According to news from the transportation sector, the station names for the future joint transportation between the Peiping-Liaoning and South Manchuria Railways are as follows: (1) Qianmen, Peiping; (2) Fengtai; (3) Langfang; (4) Tianjin; (5) Tanggu; (6) Tangshan; (7) Guye; (8) Luanzhou; (9) Changli; (10) Qinhuangdao; (11) Yuguan; (12) Jinzhou; (13) Goubangzi; (14) Dahushan; (15) Huanggu Village; (16) Shenyang; (17) Tieling; (18) Kaiyuan; (19) Gongzhuling; (20) Changchun. Changchun is the terminus of the South Manchuria Railway. After the Russo-Japanese War, its north was named North Manchuria and its south South Manchuria. Changchun is located at the crossroads of the three provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, and Heilongjiang, and its trade scope extends to the entire Northeast. (2nd)

Red Bandits Infest Datian 87

They Entered the City for Three Days and Then Withdrew

Salt and Rice are Extremely Scarce in the Bandit Area

Xiamen Dispatch: The Red bandits' Northern Route Army urgently attacked Shicheng and Ninghua, and the Eastern Route Army advanced from Liancheng, preparing a general attack on Changting, their last lair, which is in a perilous situation. At the end of last month, Zhu and Mao convened a military conference in Changting. Later, Zhu and Mao returned to Ruijin, and Peng Dehuai stayed in Changting. This month, the Communist bandits changed their strategy of stubbornly holding out and attempting to break through the rear, diverting the Central Army forces attacking the bandit lairs in Ninghua and Changting. On the 16th of this month, the Red bandits' Luo Binghui department broke through and fled to the Yang Yutang area northeast of Liancheng, then fled to the Shi Tao Market in Ningyang. The Central Army and the 14th Security Regiment pursued and intercepted them, and bombed them with airplanes. They then fled northeast to the northwest of Ningyang, and on the 18th, they arrived at Taoyuan Market in Datian County. The bandit leader was Chen Kaifa. Datian's defense forces only had the security regiment, which was no match. Therefore, on the 20th, they captured Datian County. Datian is located east of Yong'an, south of Youxi and Shaxian, and north of Yongchun and Dehua. The area is quite important. The Eastern Route Headquarters ordered the garrison forces in Yong'an and Shaxian, and the Dehua [missing text] Division [missing text] Brigade, to launch a three-pronged attack on Datian. However, the bandits who captured Datian only stayed in the city for three days, and on the 23rd, they abandoned the city and retreated. Chen Jing, the Datian County magistrate, fled to Dehua when the bandits captured the city. Shen Fazao happened to be personally supervising the [missing text] regiment and the 5th Security Regiment in Dehua to suppress the local bandit Chen Gongliang. Shen sent [missing text] regiment and part of the [missing text] Security Regiment to patrol and intercept the bandits on the border of Datian to prevent the bandits from fleeing south. Chen Jing was delayed in Dehua due to obstructing the water flow, and arrived in Quanzhou on the 26th. He will transfer to Fuzhou to report to the provincial government. Shen attacked Chen Gongliang's bandit lair, Dazheng Village, in Dehua and recaptured it on the 26th. Chen's troops were routed, and Chen's whereabouts are unknown. On the 27th, Shen learned from scouts that the Datian bandits had abandoned the city and retreated on the 23rd, and order in Datian was gradually being restored. Shen ordered Tan Xuede, the director of the Southern District Security Branch, to lead the [missing text] regiment and the [missing text] Security Regiment to patrol in Datian. The bandits from Datian split into groups and fled between Datian, Youxi, Yong'an, and Shaxian. The Central Army from upstream has dispatched teams to intercept and suppress them. However, the Red bandits' outward flight is not enough to resolve the crisis in their remaining bandit areas. According to refugees who recently fled from the Changting bandit area to Longyan, days ago, some bandit troops left Changting to flee elsewhere, seemingly moving towards Liancheng (referring to the aforementioned bandits fleeing to Datian). Currently, the Changting city hosts the pseudo-Fujian Soviet government, stationed with 200-300 Red Guards. There is no shortage of food, with each national currency buying about four dou of rice, and six to seven jin of pork per yuan. However, salt is extremely scarce, with only six liang purchasable per yuan. The most scarce items in the bandit area are salt, matches, and kerosene. The so-called "Red Army" is the most privileged in the bandit area. Previously, each person could receive seven qian of salt and eight matches per day, but now they can only receive three qian of salt and four matches. The general populace barely has any salt and often preserves fire, showing their predicament. Furthermore, according to Li Jingshen, the [missing text] regiment commander of the Ningyang Security [missing text] Battalion, a bandit scout captured by villagers in Chishui Township had a leather bag confiscated containing 12 cash coins, a small green note, and a piece of red cloth plaster. According to the confession, the items carried were scout identification marks. A notice has been sent to all jurisdictions. In addition, there are recently hidden groceries worth 20,000 yuan in the mountains of the Jin Feng district of Yongding. The Security [missing text] Regiment reported this and requested that a team be dispatched to search and suppress them. Goods used in the bandit area mostly enter the bandit area from Dapu and Yongding via Shanghang. The Eastern and Southern Routes are currently working together to strictly seal off the area. (July 30th)

Northwest Inspection Notes by Our Special Correspondent Geng Ya 88

From Lanzhou to Xining

On the morning of the 21st, I departed from Lanzhou, hiring a "jia wozi" from the Tiancheng shop. A "jia wozi," also known as a "shanzi," uses two mules walking in front and behind, carrying double poles with a sedan chair frame in the middle. There is a bamboo mat on top and a rope net below, which can be used to lay out boxes, bedding, and rugs. People can sit or lie on it. There were five "jia wozi" traveling together and over ten pack horses, transporting cigarettes under pressure for an Anglo-American tobacco company. The porters delayed due to added cargo, which displeased the company people, causing a great commotion. The journey started at ten o'clock. Leaving the city and crossing Leituan Bridge, there were four beggars lying and smoking opium in a vacant lot behind a monument. Their figures were emaciated and their condition was ugly. The opium poppy flowers in the fields had withered, and the seed pods were full. Tobacco leaves were planted between them, already two or three inches tall. The wheat ears had already turned yellow, and the harvest was not far off. The road was sunken, with earthen banks on both sides. Dust accumulated four or five inches deep on the road. When the wind blew, the dust flew up, blinding and suffocating. I walked on the bank road on both sides, talking to the Anglo-American tobacco company employees. I learned that there were six people in their group, including two Englishmen, one the son of a royal brigadier and the other a major capitalist. They are currently managers of the Tianjin and Zhangjiakou branches respectively. They do not shy away from the hardship of long journeys, but are willing to devote themselves to promoting their company's products. Although it is said to be their duty, their attention to and investigation of the situation in our interior is something that our country's merchants cannot hope to match.

The villages along the way used well water. The wells were eight or nine zhang deep and used a two-tiered pulley system to draw water. First, a circular pit about two zhang in diameter and three or four zhang deep was dug. Then, at the bottom of the pit, a well was dug down to the spring, four or five zhang deep. The well was lined with stones in a rectangular shape three feet long and two feet wide. Two rotating wooden wheels were placed on the opening, one vertical and one horizontal, with interlocking teeth. The horizontal wheel was turned by horsepower, which also rotated the vertical wheel, and the water was drawn up. In level areas, a cart must be set up separately, repeating the process twice before the water rises to ground level and is channeled to irrigate the fields. It can be seen that digging a well is very laborious and drawing water is quite difficult. The lack of water sources in Long Province is a major reason for the decline of agriculture.

Twenty li to Cui's Cliff, there is a temple called Baiyun Guan (White Cloud Temple). The halls and pavilions rise from the ground and are stacked on top of each other, reaching straight to the mountain peak. The atmosphere is lofty and admirable. The surveying team of the Gansu Land Surveying Bureau was there. The bureau is divided into three sections: topography, cartography, and ordinary surveying. The topography section is further divided into boundary and leveling groups. The entire province of Gansu was originally planned to be surveyed in ten years. However, due to financial difficulties, I am afraid it will not be completed on schedule. There are over 300 households in Cui's Cliff, with many people and little land. Each person owns an average of only half a mu. Each mu yields about one dou (each dou weighing 120 jin), which is not enough to eat. People rely on doing odd jobs, rafting, or peddling to alleviate the agricultural distress. Further on to Chenguanying and Gucheng, waterwheels were placed along the river. The wheel diameter is about five zhang. The original river water power is used to continuously rotate the wheels. Small buckets are obliquely attached to the wheel rim, scooping water and turning upwards, pouring it into a trough to irrigate the fields, which is quite convenient. Sandy fields are planted with tobacco, and earthen fields are planted with wheat. A good harvest is possible, truly the fertile land of western Long. There are many date gardens in Gucheng, with the green shade covering the sun. Walking through it is cool and comfortable.

Thirty li to Xiliugou. Villagers are devoting all their resources to building a tall temple, with new couplets on the pillars, saying "To mend the sky's hole, the hearts of all have repaired the Three Officials' Hall; to continue the earth's vein, harmonious minds have created the Five-Story Building." Reading it, I see only its empty and absurd intentions, and can imagine the height of the building. If such superstition is not eliminated, the rural economy will have one more invisible leak. It can be asserted. Moreover, I see many young men and women still wearing queues and bound feet. To cut them off and liberate them, it seems that a simple proclamation will not be effective. Walking west along the river, the high mountains to the north and south stretch for dozens of li, narrowing from wide to narrow, embracing to form a mouth. The river water rushes down, the sound like ten thousand horses galloping. Passing through the mouth, it widens into a peaceful plain. Fruit gardens are planted with walnuts, dates, apricots, plums, pears, etc., with fruitful results. It can quench thirst. We arrived in Xincheng and stayed the night, traveling 70 li. The two Englishmen, Mr. Ba, and their companions had dinner, with a wide variety of foods, as luxurious as usual. Villagers gathered to watch, seemingly drooling. In fact, their rich meals are the cream and blood of our compatriots who love foreign cigarettes. There are 200 households in Xincheng, mostly self-cultivating farmers, followed by small-scale business operators.

On the 22nd, we departed from Xincheng. Five li to Qingshiguan, leaning on the dangerous cliff to the left and facing the deep abyss to the right. It is quite important in western defense. Because it is paddy field here, it can be cultivated twice a year. Opium poppies and wheat in the spring, and millet, tobacco, sorghum, and cotton in the autumn. However, cotton must be planted every other year for the soil to be fertile. Each mu pays five jiao in silver in the spring and three sheng of grain in the autumn. Renting land costs ten yuan per year. In the morning, the river water was light yellow, but suddenly turned red at noon, probably due to heavy rain upstream, causing mountain torrents to erupt. The river is getting smaller and smaller to the south, even as small as only three or five zhang, but because the mountain cliffs embrace together, the water flow is unusually turbulent. Twenty li to Shansi Gulch. On the opposite bank is Dajia Gulch, where we crossed. The ferry fare is forty large (copper coins) per person, 1,000 for livestock, and 100 for donkeys. Each boat carries both people and horses, earning about 200 yuan per month. According to the boatman, "Yan Yunting, a gentleman in Xincheng, is greedily monopolizing the ferry fees in the name of public use, which is very hateful. The Yellow River ferry cannot be crossed during the rapid water of July and August. In winter and early spring, the ice prevents boats from traveling. The ferry operates for a maximum of five or six months each year. After deducting labor costs, the remainder is very meager, but Yan gets rich without lifting a finger. The suffering does not earn money, the money-making suffers no hardship, there is nothing more unfair in the world than this." As the boat approached the other shore, the Englishmen gave cigarettes to the boatmen, frequently asking if they were good. The boatmen competed to smoke them, praising them endlessly. I watched silently for a long time, feeling a slight pain in my heart.

There are 200 households in Dajia Gulch, all with the surname Da. Every year on the second day of the second lunar month, they go to the Da Hua household's tomb once, slaughtering pigs and sheep to pay homage to the ancestral tomb. The old and young gather to eat, all over the mountains and fields. This is called "Qingming Festival Wine," and it is a grand gathering held annually by the entire village. In recent years, the village chiefs and leaders often use their authority to collect money, falsely reporting expenses, causing lawsuits to arise, and feelings have deteriorated. According to locals, the dry land in the village is planted every other year, and nine out of ten harvests fail. It is said that no "crops" have been harvested since 1927. Grain taxes are still paid as usual, about ten yuan per dou. Because there is no yield from the fields, people mostly use wages to pay, or even borrow to live. Borrowing one yuan in February or March requires repaying four liang of tobacco in June or July (the market price is two liang per yuan). Those who lend money are local tyrants and evil gentry, and those who are exploited are small and medium-sized poor farmers. The village has a primary school with about 40 students. Each student's tuition ranges from one to five yuan. The teacher receives about 100 yuan in salary per year. The textbooks used are mixed with classics and Chinese language. Students only know how to recite sentences and do not understand the meaning of the words. Furthermore, a farmer recounted, "I have seven mu of land. If I plant wheat, I only harvest one shi and four dou, worth about seventy yuan. If I plant opium poppies, I can harvest five hundred liang, worth about two hundred and fifty yuan. After deducting fifty yuan for grain tax and two thousand ma zha (a type of fertilizer), worth sixty yuan, there are still one hundred and forty yuan left. Therefore, people mostly plant tobacco and do not plant wheat." He also said, "Ordinary farmers, if they encounter a bad year, will suffer from hunger and cold. The strong all go out to work or join the army. It is said that people feed the land, not the land feeding the people."

Major Flooding in Guangxi Province

Multiple Sections of the Highway Were Washed Away 89

Roadbeds and Bridges Collapsed, Traffic Was Blocked

Losses in Yong, Long, Wu and Other Areas Exceeded 100,000

Guangzhou Dispatch: At the beginning of July this year, heavy rains fell in the southern provinces, and major flooding occurred in the three rivers of Guangdong Province, resulting in considerable losses. Guangxi Province has high mountains and shallow rivers, with flash floods erupting and rivers overflowing. Many agricultural products have been submerged, and the highways that have been built in various prefectures have been particularly damaged. Heavy rains have continued to fall in recent days, and accumulated water has not receded, causing traffic on various roads to be blocked. Damage to roadbeds and bridges has been particularly severe. Recently, the Guangxi Provincial Highway Bureau received reports of flood damage from various areas as follows: (1) Yongning District: A. Sections of the road near Yong City: The water submerged the Shajiang Bridge surface by about five feet, and the Yuanjiang Bridge was also submerged by more than one foot. B. The old bridge near Wutang in Yongbin and the Sanba Bridge near Taishou Market were completely washed away. A section of bridge was washed away and several sections of the roadbed were damaged near Batang. The western end of Kunlun hillside collapsed, and mud and stones filled the ditches and road surface, measuring over seven feet. Soil collapsed from the top of Pingyang'ao Mountain onto the road surface, making it impassable. Sections of the road near Liudong were washed out by the water, measuring over 700 feet in length. The stone collapse from Dongjiang Bridge to Hongniao'ao was the most severe, measuring over 60 feet long. Mud and rocks blocked the road surface, measuring over 20 feet wide. A 3,000-foot long section of roadbed was washed away from Hongniao'ao to Silong, especially the section from Silong to Taishou, where over 1,000 feet of road surface was washed away. A 2,000-foot section of road surface was destroyed from Taishou Market to Binyang. The roadbeds at both ends of the Baxiu Bridge were washed away, measuring about 400 feet long. The roadbeds at both ends of the Shigao Bridge collapsed, measuring 500 feet long. The temporary stone banks and roadbeds at both ends of the Sanba Bridge were also washed away, measuring 78 feet long. C. On the Bin-Gui road, the roadbed west of the Saoba Bridge was washed away, four feet deep and over 50 li long. Over a hundred feet of roadbed was washed away at the Gongzhang Bridge head. Although iron wires were added to bind the beams of the Dianxing Bridge when the water was about to submerge it, the force of the water was too strong and it was broken, and the bridge surface floated away. The bridges at Leijiu, Huanglian, and Qili were all submerged by water, four, five, six or seven feet deep, and many sections of roadbed were damaged. D. On the Binqian road, over a hundred feet of roadbed was washed away at the Changche Bridge head. Zouxu and nearby villages and fields were turned into swamps. The sections of the road submerged by water were six or seven feet deep and three or four thousand feet long. Over 10,000 feet of road surface were submerged in the areas of Bada, Longtan, and Guxian. E. On the Yongqin route, the Nahe and Pangjiang rivers rose sharply and surged. The stone walls on both sides of the river bridge were washed away, and the bridge surface floated away with the water, preventing people and vehicles from crossing. The rest of the road surface was also severely damaged. (2) Longzhou District: A. On the Yonglong road, in the Mingjiang section, mountain floods flowed horizontally and the river water rose sharply, causing a lot of damage to the road surface and roadbed. B. In the Longnan section, most of the roads from the Yuehua boundary to the Zhennanguan Dui Pan Shu Road were washed away. A culvert near Fengliujie was washed away, and no less than twenty landslides occurred along the road, with mud and stones filling the road surface. C. On the section from Longzhou to Shuikou, the stone bridge near the village entrance was washed away. Two zhang of the stone road near Luohui collapsed, measuring five or six feet wide and deep. The roadbed near Wayao was also damaged by several feet. (3) Wuzhou District: A. The Jinji Bridge on the Gui-Xing-Yu road was once submerged by water to a depth of over three feet and a width of over ten li, and many sections of roadbed and road surface were washed away nearby. According to the statistics, the mountain floods caused losses of about 100,000 yuan to highway bridges in the Yong, Long, Gui, and Wu districts, while other losses have not yet been estimated. (July 30th)

Tianjin

Franco-Japanese Competition for Concessions 90

Filling Pits with Soil and Forcibly Seizing Land

Developing Night Markets to Compete for Prosperity

Tianjin Dispatch: The authorities of the French Concession in Tianjin have recently been forcibly expanding their territory towards Lao Xikai, and have decided to implement various taxes and establish a Chinese Taxpayer Association on January 1st of next year, as previously reported. It is now heard that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is paying close attention to this matter and has determined that it cannot be resolved through negotiations with the Tianjin Municipal Government alone. Therefore, it is planned that the Ministry will gather materials and directly protest to the French Minister. The Tianjin Municipal Government has already received an order from the Ministry to investigate everything and report it to the Ministry for negotiation purposes. The French side is not concerned about our future protests and is actively developing Lao Xikai, expediting the organization of roads, the construction of streets, and the establishment of water wells. Adjacent to Lao Xikai, there was originally a pit occupying six to seven hundred mu of land, belonging to the Second District of our Township. Since last month, the French authorities, wishing to expand the Lao Xikai urban area, have ordered sanitation trucks within the concession to transport dirty soil every day to fill the pit. However, the land is located to the left of the Haiguang Temple barracks within the concession. Seeing the ambition of the French Concession, the Japanese side is unwilling to be outdone and has also ordered sanitation trucks within their concession to transport soil for filling in the same manner, both aiming to turn the water area into land and expand their respective concessions. Although our Municipal Government has learned of this matter, it has not been able to protest because they are only dumping dirty soil within their own territories and there is no obvious encroachment. However, it is expected that this will lead to further trouble in the future.

Currently, among the concessions in Tianjin, the French Concession is the most prosperous due to the two Tianjin Incidents. Amusement parks and commercial centers are everywhere. Most of the large department stores have moved from Hebei or the Japanese Concession. The area around Majiakou and 27th Road is bustling every night, resembling a city that never sleeps, with crowds of people thronging the streets throughout the night. The highest price for land within the concession is over 20,000 yuan per mu, and even in quieter areas, it reaches around 10,000 yuan. For example, the 39 mu of land belonging to the Tianjin Naval Medical School is worth over 500,000 yuan, even though it is not located in the city center. The soaring land prices make it difficult to purchase land, and currently, demand exceeds supply. Second to the French Concession is the Japanese Concession, but after the Tianjin Incident, its prosperity shifted to the French Concession. In the past year, the Japanese side has been trying to revive its economy, so they have established a night market on Asahi Street. Every evening at six o'clock, stalls fill the street, and pedestrians mingle. The items displayed are either opium smoking paraphernalia or various gambling tools. Although the appearance is lively, most visitors simply look and leave. As a result, the night market's effect is simply to add more trouble for the police. Next is the British Concession, which has a larger area and a more dignified attitude, without competition, resembling the demeanor of a gentleman. While the Japanese and French Concessions compete for prosperity, this gentleman maintains his traditional integrity and does not seek rapid advancement. The most unsuccessful but still competitive concession is the Italian Concession. Due to its remote location, it is difficult to develop. The Italian Concession authorities rack their brains to find ways to develop, such as building a jai alai court and allowing White Russians to set up roulette gambling dens, all as means of attracting customers. However, due to its unsuitable location, which is not a commercial area, the results are minimal. (1st)

### Songjiang Eighth District Chief Requests Thorough Investigation of Surtax 91

Ye Zongcheng, Director of the First Land Tax Collection Office of this county, was previously detained for embezzlement in the case of converting farmland into grain transport. After being accused by Lu Boxin and others, the magistrate ordered Ye to be detained pending verification, as reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the Eighth District Chief of this county has jointly petitioned the county government for a thorough investigation of the surtax. The original petition stated: "Land tax is the lifeblood of the entire county, and its collection depends on capable individuals. It has been heard that Ye Zongcheng, Director of the First Land Tax Collection Office of this county, has been detained for investigation due to suppressing the conversion of grain. Whether or not he has embezzled funds is uncertain. However, it has been observed that the actual collection of surtax in recent years has only reached 30%. The district chiefs have inquired with the local police in each district and found many discrepancies, which do not match the amount of regular tax collected. If there is a shortfall in regular tax, the surtax is unlikely to be spared. A resolution was passed at the ninth administrative meeting to dispatch officials for investigation, but it has not been implemented. The district chiefs believe that the shortfall in surtax affects the progress of various undertakings. Now that Director Ye is suspected of embezzlement, Your Honor should thoroughly investigate the matter to deter future occurrences. Your Honor's discernment will not allow any wrongdoers to escape justice. We, the district chiefs, and the people of the district eagerly await Your Honor's clear instructions."

###巡官瀆職被扣 Negligent Patrol Officer Detained 92

This county's public security organization was reorganized in accordance with orders, with branch offices established in autonomous regions and watch posts in other market towns. However, since the reorganization, many patrol officers in various places have been accused of misconduct, especially Gu Sen, the patrol officer of Caojing, who was accused by local residents of privately handling homicide cases and accepting bribes, perverting the law. After the county government sent personnel to investigate in the countryside and confirmed the accusations, they reported back to the county. County Magistrate Jin was furious and immediately ordered Director He to summon the negligent patrol officer and detain him. Director He followed the order and telegraphed Gu Patrol Officer to come to the bureau and ordered him to be detained.

This county's party headquarters has always been extremely diligent in handling social undertakings. ###蘇州蘇常公路即可通車 Suzhou-Changshu Highway Soon to Open 94

The Suzhou-Changshu Highway, jointly constructed by Wu County and Changshu, will be open to traffic in mid-August. The Suzhou Construction Bureau is currently planning to complete the Louqi section of the Suzhou ring road. At the same time, the Suzhou-Mudu Road, located in the scenic western suburbs of Wuzhong, is being invested in and constructed by the Sufu Long-Distance Bus Company, aiming to be completed and open to traffic on Double Ten Day (October 10th). Plans are also underway to open up a connection to the Sumu Road to directly reach the Dongshan of Taihu Lake. The Mudong Road has already been surveyed once, with a planned length of 24 li and an estimated construction cost of approximately 100,000 yuan. Simultaneously, preparations are being made to construct the Hutong Road between Huguan and Tongan Bridge, leading directly from Huguan to Suzhou.

###水陸警探搜查土棧 Police Search Land Opium Dens 95

Although opium prohibition in Suzhou appears to have been eliminated on the surface, opium dens still operate as usual. The other day, four ruffians went to the Guo Baofeng opium den opened by Guo Yushi in Cao Hu Xu Lane and demanded protection money. They were refused. Unwilling to accept this, the ruffians lingered outside the door. The opium den then sent out more than ten people, dragged the ruffians to the Tianfulou teahouse, and severely beat them. The four ruffians all suffered serious injuries. Later, through mediation, they were given compensation for their injuries, and the matter was settled. Shao Heng, a detective from the Water Police, was demoted. The other day, in Fengqiao Town, three li from the city, he caught an opium trafficker named Zhang Yingqing (also known as Zhang Aqi) and seized 116 taels and three qian of opium. He immediately escorted him to the Second District of the Public Security Bureau in Mu. Zhang confessed in the district department that he had bought the opium from the Guo Baofeng opium den. Thereupon, District Chief Lou dispatched a large number of detectives, together with the land police, to search the Guo Baofeng opium den. Because the opium den had heard of the search in advance, they moved the evidence elsewhere, so nothing was found at the time. Only one associate of the opium den, Huang Zhongyi, was apprehended and taken to the district, where Zhang Rongqing identified him. Section Chief Feng interrogated him and ordered him to be detained. He will be sent to the court for interrogation today. The Wang Public Security Bureau believes that the police officer in charge and the branch chief are suspected of colluding and shielding the opium den and has decided to investigate.

###息借田賦發放欠餉 Borrowing on Land Tax to Pay Back Wages 96

The Wu County Public Security Bureau is in arrears with police wages for five months, totaling over 90,000 yuan. Recently, on August 1st, a new system was implemented, and the laid-off police officers urgently need to be paid their back wages for severance. Thereupon, Director Wang submitted a request to the county government to find ways to raise funds. Yesterday, County Magistrate Wu invited Chairman Shi of the County Chamber of Commerce to the government to discuss the matter. As a result, it was decided that the County Chamber of Commerce would invite the leaders of the banking, money exchange, and land industries to discuss borrowing 66,000 yuan, using the land tax for the 23rd year as collateral, with a term of six months and a monthly interest rate of 1.2%.

###救濟院總辭職 Resignation of the entire Relief Institute 97

Dan Shusheng, Director of the Wu County Relief Institute, Chen Xilian, Deputy Director, and others, yesterday (3rd) jointly submitted a letter of resignation to the county government. County Magistrate Wu decided to retain them.

###無錫鐵路橋開鑿水槽 Opening a Water Channel in Wuxi Railway Bridge 98

The county government previously received a joint petition from Hua Lunxiang and others, the township chiefs of Zhoujing and other lower-level townships in the Second District, to dredge the railway bridge at No. 149 Zhoujing Lane to facilitate irrigation. After receiving the petition, County Magistrate Yan sent a letter to the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations to discuss the matter. After the letter was sent, it was reported that the Engineering Department had been ordered to instruct the Dan-Su Section Chief to find a way to dredge the channel. According to the report, excavating the bottom of the bridge, which is entirely made of cement, would endanger traffic safety, but in order to protect farmland water conservancy, a six-foot-wide water channel will be excavated in the middle of the bridge bottom, which will not endanger the bridge piers, and the water flow will be unobstructed. After receiving the letter, the county government has ordered District Chief Yuan Yongshang of the Second District to inform the township chiefs.

###澄救旱會實測運河水量 Measuring Water Volume in Canals of Chenghsi Drought Relief 99

Since Cheng and Xi counties jointly worked on drought relief and opened up key passages connecting rivers and lakes, the water volume in the inner rivers has increased, benefiting a large number of farmers. It is learned that Jiangyin has already installed 50-horsepower engines at Huangtiangang and Huangshangang to pump river water into the inner rivers, and seven 24-horsepower engines are distributed in the inner rivers to receive the water, resulting in significant results. At the point where the rivers and lakes diverge, which is located at the Si River Estuary, the river tide has now reached the south of Shichuang, only three or four li away from Baitang. Since Wangting, Shadungang, and Jinsha Lock in Wuxi were opened, the water volume in the inner rivers has greatly increased, and farmland can now be irrigated. Yesterday, the Chenghsi Drought Relief Committee dispatched Zhang Lanqing to conduct an on-site survey along the canal. It has been measured that the water volume at Baitangwei and Gaoqiao is 3.5 feet, while at the northern part of Gaoqiao, a place called Vortex Water, it is 6.5 feet.

###常州部委蒞常辦理保釋假釋獄犯 Commissioners Come to Changzhou to Handle Bail and Parole for Prisoners 100

After Luo Wengan, Minister of Justice, inspected the judicial detention centers in Su, Chang, and Xi counties, he realized that the detention centers were overcrowded, and due to the extreme heat this summer, the hygiene of the detainees was bound to be greatly affected. He ordered the counties to find ways to relieve the situation and specially dispatched commissioners Li Zhaoming, together with Prosecutor Zhu Jun of the High Court, to the counties to handle the matter. Commissioners Li and Zhu arrived in Changzhou from Xi yesterday (2nd) and stayed at the Dacheng Hotel. They investigated and inquired about everything from the county court, the county government, and the detention centers, and decided to establish a Bail and Parole Review Committee at the county court. On the morning of the 3rd, they convened a meeting to review those who qualified for bail for immediate release, and those who qualified for parole would be taken to the Ministry of Justice for review before instructions were issued for separate implementation. The handling in Changzhou will take about four or five days, and they will also need to go to Danyang to handle this matter before returning to the Ministry to report.

###鎭江規定女生服裝 Zhenjiang Stipulates Dress Code for Female Students 101

The Jiangsu Department of Education, in view of the inconsistent clothing of female students in various schools throughout the province, and the fact that some students are competing to be fashionable and are engaging in decoration, which is not appropriate for education and morality, intends to rectify the situation and stipulate the style of clothing for female students in various schools. The measures are currently being drafted. Chairman Chen is also very concerned about this plan and has personally drafted several measures for the Department of Education to refer to: (1) Hair should not be permed, and the longest length should not exceed the forehead; (2) No face powder or rouge is allowed; (3) Eyebrows must not be shaved, and chests must not be exposed; (4) Clothes, trousers, skirts, etc., should have a reasonable width and should not be too tight. There are regulations on the length of clothes.

###查獲大宗烟土 Seizure of a Large Quantity of Opium 102

Xu Shenchu, Director of the First Branch of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, received a secret report yesterday (2nd) morning around 8:00 am that a large quantity of opium was being transported by dirt cart through the territory to the countryside for sale. He immediately dispatched several police officers to investigate in the Gangzixia Wufengkou area. He saw three or four dirt carts that looked suspicious and immediately ordered them to stop. Upon inspection, he found hemp sacks wrapped around the outside, and inside were two white cloth bags of crushed wheat. The sacks were sealed and taken to the bureau, where Director Xu personally inspected them one by one in public. There were thirteen bags in total, each containing forty cakes, weighing approximately 660 taels in total. Two opium traffickers, Xu Zhigui and Wang Guofu, and a cart driver, Cui Daji, were arrested on the spot. After interrogation, they confessed to selling opium. Director Xu tightly sealed the seized items and sent them to the General Bureau for verification.

###高郵肉票圖逃遭匪槍殺 Kidnapped Hostage Shot Dead While Trying to Escape 103

Chen Xinghe, a resident of Gaoyou, 51 years old, and manager of the Hengshun Clothing Store in Xinghua, was kidnapped by bandits in Nansong Village, the Fourth District, while returning from tomb-sweeping this spring, and was held in Shuangju Village, the Fifth District, for three months. He was shot dead by bandits while trying to escape by swimming. The bandits have sent a letter to his family demanding 1,000 yuan to redeem the body.

###紹興亢旱不雨 Shaoxing Suffers Severe Drought 104

縣府擬開放曹娥閘 County Government Plans to Open Cao'e Lock

The Shaoxing County Government, due to the recent hot weather and severe drought, in order to relieve the farmland in the Third District, plans to open the Cao'e Lock of the Second Dam for irrigation. However, because the lock has been in disrepair for years and is blocked both internally and externally, preventing it from being opened and closed, it has specifically requested the Tangzha Bureau Engineer Dong, together with Section Chief Zhu of the Construction Department, to inspect the lock on the 3rd to determine a solution.

並通令各機關下半旗誌哀 And Ordered All Agencies to Fly Flags at Half-Mast

###張定璠昨返滬 Zhang Dingfan Returned to Shanghai Yesterday 106

在港曾謁胡漢民 Visited Hu Hanmin in Hong Kong

中央社云、中委陳嘉佑·張定璠·及潘旦明·等一行三人、於前月南下、分赴港粤、訪晤胡漢民·陳濟棠·蕭佛成·等、有所洽商、業已公畢、潘氏前已先行返滬、張氏則於三日晨八時三十分、乘大來輪船公司克利扶總統號輪抵滬、據其抵滬時在輪次語中央社記者云、本人此次南下、純係私人行動、抵港曾謁胡展堂、抵省曾分訪陳伯南·蕭佛成·等、亦屬私人會晤、未及政治等問題、胡氏現仍居港、閉門寫讀、痔瘡已愈、血壓亦平復、西南各領袖、對五全會之召開、期望甚切、惟以距開會之期尚遥、故對西南代表出席等問題、尚未議及、西南兩機關裁撤問題、是否將來提交五全大會中討論、亦未聞有决定、張氏又謂、本人離粤已久、此次南下、覺粤省建設事業業進行殊速、反滬當作休息、入京赴贛日期、現皆未定、 According to the Central News Agency, a group of three people, including Central Committee members Chen Jiayou, Zhang Dingfan, and Pan Danming, went south last month to Hong Kong and Guangdong to visit Hu Hanmin, Chen Jitang, Xiao Focheng, and others for discussions. The mission has been completed. Mr. Pan had already returned to Shanghai earlier, while Mr. Zhang arrived in Shanghai at 8:30 am on the 3rd aboard the President Cleveland of the Da Lai Shipping Company. According to what he told the Central News Agency reporter on the ship upon his arrival in Shanghai, his trip south was purely a private matter. He visited Hu Zhantang in Hong Kong and Chen Bonan and Xiao Focheng in Guangdong, but these were also private meetings and did not touch on political issues. Mr. Hu is still residing in Hong Kong, reading in seclusion. His hemorrhoids have healed, and his blood pressure has also stabilized. The leaders of the Southwest are very eager for the convening of the Fifth Plenary Session, but since the meeting is still far away, the issue of Southwest representatives attending has not yet been discussed. It has not been heard whether the issue of abolishing the two Southwest agencies will be submitted to the Fifth Plenary Session for discussion. Mr. Zhang also said that he has been away from Guangdong for a long time and that he felt that the construction projects in Guangdong Province are progressing very quickly. He will take his return to Shanghai as a rest, and the date of his trip to Beijing and Jiangxi is currently undecided.

He went to Geneva in April with An Fuguo, the labor representative, and Wang Zhisheng, the capital representative. At the opening of the conference, he gave a detailed account of the labor administration situation in China and the recent efforts to promote the Factory Law, which received the goodwill and support of the member states of the League of Nations. Therefore, he was elected with 60 votes in this re-election of the council. Since China joined the League of Nations in 1919, representatives from previous sessions have made considerable efforts to be elected to the council, but due to the difficulty of gaining sympathy from the member states, they have never been elected. This election is not only of great expectation for the future promotion of labor administration in China but also has earned considerable honor in improving the international status. After inspecting factory inspections in Britain and France, Representative Li returned to China on the Conte Verde from Venice on the 11th of last month and is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 10:30 am today (4th). It is now heard that the labor circles in Beijing, Shanghai, Tianjin, and Wuhan have sent telegrams to express their congratulations. When Representative Li returns to China, there will be a grand welcome meeting. Various groups in this city, including the National Federation of Commerce, the Chinese Seven Industries Federation, the City Chamber of Commerce, the Mechanical Federation, and the General Labor Union, will send representatives to the New Customs Wharf to welcome the representatives to the International Labor Conference. The various groups will also hold regular banquets and invite the representatives to report on the conference.

銀行同業公會議决 Resolution of the Bankers Association

Request to Amend the Savings Bank Law 113

To Protect Depositors' Interests

Deeply Feeling Impeded and Difficult to Implement

According to Xinsheng News Agency, after the promulgation of the Savings Bank Law, the Banking Association contributed opinions, requesting the government to adopt them, and presented the difficulties of implementation to the Minister of Finance. Now that all banks have been ordered to implement it, the association held a meeting at 2:30 PM yesterday specifically to discuss the Savings Bank Law and resolved to petition the government to amend it. Attendees at yesterday's meeting included Chen Guangfu, Song ZiLiang, Jing Runyou, Wu Yunzhai, Le Gengrong, Hu Bijiang, Tang Shoumin, Ye Fuxiao, Luo Qinghua, Chen Zheqing, Chen Shizhen, Wang Zhixin, Zhu Zikui, Sun Jingxi, Wang Boyuan, Qi Yunqing, Hu Xi'an, Liu Huizhi, Xu Boming, Wu Weiru, etc. The Secretary-General, Lin Kanghou, was also present. Chen Guangfu chaired the meeting, reporting on the members' compliance with Article 9 of the Savings Bank Law as ordered by the Ministry of Finance, and the process of presenting requests for amendments to Minister Kong. The discussion then began on (1) Article 7 (Original): Savings banks, when conducting the business stipulated in Article 9, shall not use their funds except in the following ways: (1) Purchasing government bonds, treasury bills, and other secured securities approved by the Ministry of Finance; (2) Lending with government bonds, treasury bills, and other secured securities approved by the Ministry of Finance as collateral; (3) Lending with real estate that has continuous and reliable income as mortgage; (4) Lending with fixed deposit certificates or passbooks from other banks as collateral; (5) Purchasing bills accepted by other banks; (6) Depositing in other banks; (7) Secured lending to rural cooperatives; (8) Lending with agricultural products as collateral. (2) Article 8 (Original): The total amount of securities issued by the same company held by a savings bank, as specified in Article 7, Clauses 1 and 2, shall not exceed one-tenth of the company's paid-up capital and reserve fund. The total amount of loans from a savings bank, as specified in Article 7, Clause 3, shall not exceed one-fifth of its total deposits. The total amount of loans from a savings bank, as specified in Article 7, Clause 4, shall not exceed one-fifteenth of its total deposits. The amount of bills purchased by a savings bank, as specified in Article 7, Clause 5, shall not exceed one-twentieth of its total deposits. The amount of deposits from a savings bank, as specified in Article 7, Clause 6, shall not exceed one-fifteenth of its total deposits, except for those with government bonds, treasury bills, and other secured securities approved by the Ministry of Finance as collateral. When ordinary banks concurrently operate savings bank business, the provisions of the preceding two paragraphs shall apply mutatis mutandis to the amount of bills accepted by the bank department for the savings department and the amount deposited. The total amount of loans from a savings bank, as specified in Article 7, Clauses 7 and 8, shall not be less than one-fifth of the total deposits. It was resolved that Articles 7 and 8 above, for the sake of protecting depositors' interests, are in fact impeded and difficult to implement, and a request should be submitted to the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, and Ministry of Finance to request amendments, including restrictions on the composition of use and funds. The telegram will be sent after review, and a committee will be appointed to review it. (3) Article 9 (Original): Savings banks should deposit at least one-quarter of their total savings deposits in the specially established vault of the Central Bank, as collateral for the repayment of savings deposits, in the form of government bonds, treasury bills, and other secured assets. All banks have now been ordered to comply with Article 9 and deposit one-quarter of their total deposits in government bonds and treasury bills with the Central Bank. It was resolved that, when requesting amendments to the entire Savings Bank Law, the provisions of Article 9 should be presented to the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, and Ministry of Finance for a temporary delay in implementation. The meeting adjourned at 4 PM. The telegram was sent out last night. It is planned to use hundreds of acres as a factory base and three hundred acres to build a model village so that overseas compatriots can return to the country to live and work. Now, the General Manager of the factory, Mr. Huang Hongjun, under the urging of overseas Chinese, is scheduled to set sail today with his wife,

Photograph of Mr. Huang Hongjun and Ms. Qu Huijian 114

Qu Huijian, on the President Cleveland, will travel to various ports in the Americas to meet with overseas Chinese, and at the same time inspect the textile industry. His wife will assist him in contacting women in the industry. It is expected that in a few months, they will return to China with a large number of overseas Chinese to develop the industry and commerce of their motherland.

Flour Prices Rise Daily 115

Large Quantities of American Flour for Sale

Market Price Still Difficult to Stabilize

According to the Central News Agency, recently, all sectors have paid close attention to the soaring rice prices. According to news from the grain industry, recently, the rising trend of flour prices has been even greater than that of rice prices. The reason for the sharp rise is not only that most wheat-producing areas in North China have suffered from water damage, resulting in a hopeless harvest, but also that other wheat-producing countries have also had poor harvests this year. However, flour is the main food source in North China, so the demand in the flour market in this city is extremely strong. Recently, more than one million bags have been sold to the Northeast and Tianjin. The government sold 400,000 bags of American flour yesterday at a price of 2.5 yuan, but the market price is still difficult to stabilize. The minimum price of wheat was 2.7 yuan, but it has recently risen to 4 yuan and continues to rise. According to the current situation, flour market prices may continue to rise without decline.

Yesterday Another Meeting of Rickshaw Merchants Was Convened 117

Because Macey Would Not Concede to Postpone for Further Discussion

The Chamber of Commerce Formed a Special Committee That Held Its First Meeting Yesterday

The Rickshaw Industry Association of the Special District of this city, dissatisfied with the Public Concession Bureau of Works and the Vehicle Affairs Committee's refusal to issue vehicle licenses and the promulgation of new regulations, which led to disputes, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Public Concession Bureau of Works separately convened rickshaw merchants for discussions yesterday. Details are recorded below.

Macey Firmly Refused 118

The rickshaw merchants of the Special District, regarding the new regulations, sent representatives to negotiate with the Public Concession Bureau of Works several times. As a result, both parties decided to form a committee to study and improve, specializing in discussing rickshaw rentals and revising regulations. At 3 PM yesterday, the Public Concession Bureau of Works held another meeting with rickshaw merchants at the Bureau. Representatives from the association, Yin Zhiling, Hou Shaoan, Ma Saisi, Pei Er, etc., were present. Those attending from the Public Concession Bureau of Works included General Manager Zhong Si, Police Superintendent Qiu Lai, Deputy Superintendent Maideng, Vehicle Committee Chairman Macey, Chinese Director Yu Qiaqing, and Office Manager He Dekui. The rickshaw merchants first presented the situation. All representatives expressed acceptance. Regarding the rickshaw rental issue in the new regulations, rickshaw merchants currently only collect 8 jiao, which is still less than the 1 jiao stipulated by the Public Concession Bureau of Works. In addition, there are leasing expenses for the contractors. Chinese Director Yu Qiaqing believed that the proposals made by the rickshaw merchants were reasonable, but Vehicle Committee Chairman Macey insisted on the already promulgated new regulations, saying there was no room for change. Therefore, discussions continued until 6 PM without any progress. It was decided to reschedule the meeting for Monday morning next week for further discussion.

Chamber of Commerce Forms Special Committee 119

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce of this city, fearing that the deadlock between the two parties would lead to a split, affecting public security, which would be significant, and that the livelihoods of tens of thousands of rickshaw pullers were even more important, specifically convened a standing committee meeting at 2 PM the day before yesterday to discuss the matter. Yu Zuoting, Jin Runxiang, Ke Ganchen, Zheng Zenan, Pan Xusheng, Ma Shaoquan, etc., were present. First, Secretary Yan E’sheng reported on the progress of the case and the new regulations promulgated by the Public Concession Bureau of Works, the attitude of the rickshaw merchants, etc. As a result of the discussion, a special committee was organized to be responsible for research and handling, and Chen Zheqing, Ma Shaoquan, Jin Runxiang, Ke Ganchen, and Yan E’sheng were appointed as committee members. At 3 PM yesterday, they convened rickshaw merchants for talks, including Gu Songmao, Zhang Jingbo, Zhu Hegao, Jin Chunlin, and Zhang Huaiyang. Special committee members of the Chamber of Commerce Jin Runxiang, Ke Ganchen, Ma Shaoquan, and Yan E’sheng were also present. Jin Runxiang chaired the meeting, discussing the four issues of rickshaws in detail: (1) Property rights, (2) Rent, (3) Registration, (4) Model. The meeting adjourned at 5 PM.

Japanese Side

No Miscellaneous Grains Shipped to Shanghai 120

Gu Sheng Yi's Talk

According to the Central News Agency, recently there has been much public talk about the grain industry in this city purchasing large quantities of foreign rice, and that the Japanese are shipping large quantities of miscellaneous grains from the Northeast to the grain industry in this city. The Central News Agency reporter specially inquired about this matter with Gu Xinyi, a giant in the grain industry, who said the following:

A Batch of Saigon Rice Has Arrived in Shanghai 121

According to Mr. Gu, the rice industry in this city did indeed order Saigon rice from Siamese rice merchants, and one thousand bags have already arrived in Shanghai. As for the report that the Local Coordination Association ordered more than 4,000 tons of Saigon rice, there is a slight misunderstanding. The Saigon rice was not ordered in the name of the Local Coordination Association, but by gentlemen from the banking industry and other industries in this city in their private capacity. It has not yet been shipped. After it arrives, it will not be sold immediately, but will be sold at a fair price next spring if rice prices soar. As for He Defu, a Siamese overseas Chinese rice merchant, he met with me and is currently in Shanghai. He is in the country to investigate rice prices, so the rice industry in this city has not traded with Mr. He. If domestic rice prices continue to rise in the future, Mr. He has agreed to ship Saigon rice back to the country to help regulate them.

No Miscellaneous Grains Shipped to Shanghai by the Japanese Side 122

Regarding the rumor that the Japanese side recently shipped a large quantity of miscellaneous grains to Shanghai for sale, Mr. Gu replied that this statement is indeed unfounded. The Northeast originally produced soybeans and red sorghum as its main products, but according to current market prices, the price of soybeans produced in the Northeast is more than 4 yuan per dan, and the price of red sorghum is nearly 3 yuan per dan, which are both more expensive than domestic prices. Soybeans are produced in Anhui, Jiangsu, and other provinces. The price of soybeans shipped from these provinces to Shanghai for sale is 3.4 yuan, which is about 1 yuan lower than the price of soybeans from the Northeast. Therefore, soybeans from the Northeast have not been shipped to Shanghai for sale for a long time. Moreover, the various miscellaneous grains produced domestically are currently sufficient for use, so there is no need for assistance from foreign miscellaneous grains. Grain merchants have also decided to prioritize the sale of domestic products, so this statement is indeed unfounded.

Page 12

Merchant Shipping, People's Livelihood Alliance Founded

Joint Sea-River Shipping Cooperation 124

Eighteen Articles of the Contract Have Been Signed

The Implementation Period Has Been Agreed to Be Six Months

Since the dissolution of the alliance of seven companies on April 1 for the Chuanshan River shipping industry, the companies have reduced shipping rates and competed for cargo. Up to now, the cotton yarn item has fallen to two yuan per piece, which is only one-tenth of the original rate. Other goods have also been reduced in price uniformly, causing no Chuanshan River shipping to be free from losses. Currently, Minsheng Company has the largest influence on the Chuanshan River shipping. The Chinese merchant ships on the Huiyi route have mostly been incorporated into Minsheng. In order to develop the business of the lower reaches of the Yangtze River and to transport goods from various coastal ports, the company's general manager, Lu Zuofu, personally came to Shanghai to negotiate with the China Merchants Bureau on joint sea-river shipping cooperation. After a long period of discussion, eighteen articles have been decided, which have been signed by the authorities of both parties and will be implemented immediately. Details are urgently reported as follows:

Cooperation Motivation: Minsheng Company has been buying more and more ships in recent years, and has secured the first position in shipping in the Chuanshan River. However, most of the ships operate between Chongqing and Yichang, followed by ships directly from Chongqing to Shanghai. In terms of business, the upstream occupies a superior position, while the downstream lacks docks and warehouses, so it cannot be fully developed. For this problem, the company has contacted various shipping companies in Shanghai for a long time, but without success. Since the state-owned China Merchants Bureau suffered an accident with the Emei ship, the upper Yangtze River shipping has suddenly felt a lack of ships, and Lu Zuofu, the general manager of Minsheng, contacted the bureau to cooperate with Yangtze River shipping, and agreed on joint sea-river shipping methods with the China Merchants Bureau. Both parties consulted for a long time before success.

Signing the Contract: The joint sea-river shipping and Yangtze River cooperation business of the two companies, under the meeting of both parties, signed a contract, a total of eighteen articles, agreed by Liu Hongsheng and Lu Zuofu. After many revisions, the formal draft was finalized on July 31. The China Merchants Bureau submitted it to the board of directors for approval. Lu Zuofu in Shanghai on the Minsheng side can be responsible for signing. Details of the cooperation and joint transportation between the two companies are still being drawn up. The joint transportation will start this month and will be valid for six months. If the results are excellent, it can be extended again.

Joint Method: The contract stipulates that from Chongqing to Hankou, and from Yuezhou, Changsha, and the lower reaches of the Yangtze River to Shanghai, and the two north and south sea routes, a total of twenty-one wheel ports of the joint river and sea shipping areas, Minsheng Company supplies the China Merchants Bureau with transportation warehouses and other items in the Yiwanyi section of Chongqing, and stipulates that Minsheng will not add ships to the Changjiang Road in Xiang'e Road, and the China Merchants Bureau will not add shifts in the Yiwanyi Line of Chongqing. The China Merchants Bureau's North and South Ocean wheels load joint transport cargo for Minsheng. The China Merchants Bureau's transfer cargo to Sichuan is also transported by Minsheng wheels. The goods shipped out of Chongqing and Yiwanyi are returned to the Minsheng bill of lading, and the goods entering Sichuan in Shanghai are signed and issued by the China Merchants Bureau.

Immediate Implementation: After the two parties finalized the contract, they discussed implementation. Minsheng Wheel arrived in Shanghai from Sichuan and has changed to mooring at the North Warehouse Wharf of the China Merchants Bureau, and the loading and unloading of goods and passengers is quite convenient. The China Merchants Bureau Chuanshan River, although there is no boat line now, can also carry passengers and goods, and can be transported on behalf of Minsheng boats. The Minsheng Company's National Wheel, which exported today, has started to jointly transport Wanxian Chongqing goods. The China Merchants Bureau, due to the success of Chuanshan River cooperation, its long-stalled China Merchants Chongqing Customs Office, Hengtai will be responsible for handling it.
